(1) I recommend becoming a member of an activist organization that promotes tolerance and social justice. One great organization 
of this kind is the Southern Poverty Law Center (SPLC). You can access this organization online at www.splcenter.org. This 
nonprofit educational and legal foundation functions as a clearing house and activist leader for social good in the United States. 
This is the group that designed โMix-It-Up-At-Lunch Day.โ They publish a magazine that members receive titled [3mTeaching Tolerance [0m. 
Every issue is full of sound tips for promoting tolerance and social activism in children. I learn something new about my fellow 
travelers on this Earth from every issue. The SPLC also makes free curriculum kits available to teachers. One example is 
โResponding to Hate at School: A Guide for Teachers, Counselors and Administrators.โ 

(2) When children are seeking activities to engage in, assist them in finding one that includes social activism. Many 
opportunities for service exist in all of our communities. One example is the Girl Scouts/Boy Scouts organization. Service to 
others is a hallmark of the work they ask of children. If you encounter a troop that is intolerant of some groups of children, 
seek another troop. Often, the Scout leadersโ views prevail and we are all on the journey of overcoming bias at different levels. 
One recent book published about Eagle Scouts was written to detail some of the service engaged in by those who have attained this 
level of Scouting. They have gone on to achieve national office, become members of the astronaut corps, save natural habitats, 
lead colleges, and serve as camp counselors as adults. Alvin Townleyโs [3mLegacy of Honor: The Values and Influence of Americaโs 
Eagle Scouts [0mwas published in 2007 by Thomas Dunne Books. 

(3) Youth Communication is a nonprofit youth development program that sells resource books for adults and adolescents, written by 
adolescents. Examples of some of their available titles are โHelping Others,โ โGrowing up Black, Asian, Latinoโ (three titles), 
โResilience,โ and โMental Health.โ Find them at www.youthcomm.org. 

(4) The Anti-Defamation League (ADL), in conjunction with Barnes and Noble publish a list of books that address social justice. 
The pamphlet they produce is called โClose the Book on Hateโ and can be downloaded at the ADLโs website: 
www.adl.org/prejudice/default/asp. This list contains books for children and adults. 

[1m(ูข) ูุชุจ ููุฃุทูุงู [0m

The childrenโs book collection of Kim and Kent Case includes the following titles: 

(1) [3mKing and King. [0mLinda de Haan and Stern Nijland. Two males become a couple. 

(2) [3mKing and King and Family. [0mLinda de Hann and Stern Nijland. A male couple adopts a child. 

(3) [3mAnd Tango Makes Three. [0mJustin Richardson and Peter Parnell. The true story of two male penguins at the Central Park Zoo who 
become a couple and raise a baby penguin together. 

(4) [3mHeather Has Two Mommies. [0mLeslea Newman. 

(5) [3mMollyโs Family. [0mNancy Garden. A kindergarten child with two moms who attend Parentsโ Night together. 

(6) [3mWe Adopted You, Benjamin Koo. [0mLinda Walvoord Girard. First person account of a child from Korea adopted in the United States. 

(7) [3mNew Moon [0mis a magazine for girls about embracing girlhood and promotes tolerance and activism. 

(8) [3mWilliamโs Doll. [0mCharlotte Zolotow. Williamโs grandmother buys him a doll so that he will learn nurturing skills. 

(9) [3mThe Sissy Duckling. [0mHarvey Fierstein. Elmer the duck enjoys traditionally feminine activities and perseveres when his friends 
deride him. 

(10) [3mMy Name was Hussein. [0mHristo Kyuchukov. Ethnic violence means that children must adopt new beliefs or even change their names 
to survive. 

(11) [3mWhat if the Zebras Lost Their Stripes? [0mJohn Reitano. Black, white, or striped, we are all in the animal kingdom together. 

(12) [3mZackโs Story: Growing Up with Same Sex Parents. [0mKeith Greenberg. A first person account of Zack, who has two moms. 

(13) [3mHappy to Be Nappy. [0mbell hooks (author bell hooks does not capitalize her name). Be proud of who you are. 

(14) [3mLetโs Talk About Race. [0mJulius Lester. Inside we are all the same. 

(15) [3mBlack is Brown is Tan. [0mArnold Adoff. A multi-ethnic family has many beautiful skin-tones. 

(16) [3mSpotty. [0mMargaret Rey. A spotted bunny leaves his all white bunny family only to find a spotted bunny family who is skeptical 
of a white bunny in their midst. 

(17) [3mTusk Tusk. [0mDavid McKee. White and black elephants fight to their deaths while the peace loving ones escape. Generations later 
the surviving elephants emerge and are all gray. 

(18) [3mWhite Socks Only. [0mEvelyn Coleman. A young African-American girl drinks from an โAll Whiteโ fountain and brings others to 
social activism as well. 

(19) [3mWhy Should I Recycle? [0mJen Green. Mr. Jones, a teacher, shows his students the benefit of recycling. 

(20) [3mABC A Family Alphabet Book. [0mBobbie Combs. Families are diverse.
